===== PAGE 1 =====
TEACH US TO NUMBER OUR DAYS —
A HIGH HOLIDAY THOUGHT
The hands on the clock of time turn inexorably. We are sometimes saddened when we realize that time
moves on, that the years are slipping by. Yet, these thoughts should not depress us.
The wisdom of living consists in making the most of what we are given. We cannot weave without
threads, but it is our skill with the threads with determines whether we shall fashion a beautiful tapestry or
labor without producing anything of worth or beauty.
God does not fashion life for us. He does not determine the shape of our dreams, or of our
accomplishments, but He gives us the threads... He has endowed our hands with energy, our minds with
power to reason, our hearts with the power to feel, and He has placed upon us the scene of nature
abounding in the raw materials with which we can build to our heart’s desire.
An artist who has spent his days fashioning a thing of beauty rejoices in his labor when it is done. He does
not fret that the days which have passed have made him older. Only empty days, futile days, wasted days
are a tragedy. Only the passing of days such as these are depressing.
How are we using the threads - the material of life which God has given us? On Rosh Hashanah we ask
this question. It is a disturbing question, because on its answer depends the sum of the meaning in our lives.
Wasted threads, badly used threads, show up in the final design. But when we weave with skill, and
fashion life into a pattern of harmony and goodness, then our existence becomes permeated with serenity
and peace. We can laugh though the days pass and the years go, for then we have given only time in
exchange for achievement.
During this season we oten recall the Psalmist’s prayer, “Teach us to number our days that we may get us
a heart of wisdom.” No -- it does not really mean to count only days. Anyone can do that. It is rather a prayer
to make the days count. That is the supreme wisdom of living.
EAST COAST FRUIT CO.
Walter Portnoy - Mrs. Louis Portnoy and Families
The above thoughts were presented by the Portnoys with the hope that it will nurture some reflection on
our most precious possession - the gift of life.

===== PAGE 3 =====
United Synagogue Youth
U. S. Y.
The general aim of the United Synagogue Youth
program is to bring about a meaningful and fully
reciprocal encounter of Judaism, the Jewish people,
and the synagogue on one side, and the Jewish
teenager on the other. As a result of this encounter
the Jewish teenager will, firstly, demonstrate and
experience how the Jewish way of living, through
study, action and fellowship leads the way to personal
fulfillment and growth while meeting his spiritual and
social needs, and secondly make a significant
contribution to his synagogue, community, society
and the Jewish people.

the Pre-School and Day School are invited to join the P.T. A. which serves as a link between parents,
teachers and the school.
Monies derived from our major fund-raising efforts are used for educational and cultural purposes
only; encyclopedia, projectors, playground equipment, bookstand, other valuable school
equipment have been donated to the schools on behalf of the P.T.A.
I ask you for your support and look forward to a most successful year.

Shirley

Center Choral Society
Directed by
Cantor Emeritus Abraham Marton
Our Cantor Emeritus, Abraham Marton, held his Choral Society Concert, and delighted the entire audience. The selection of
music, the professional manner in which it was presented, and the entire program was a delight for all who were there. We were
enthralled with the wide range of voices and everyone rose and ebbed with each strain. It is indeed our good fortune to have
Cantor Marton, who is still our leading force in Jewish music at the Jacksonville Jewish Center, and we wish him many more
years and many more concerts. Outstanding Center talents, Raymond Cohen, tenor and sopranoes, Rosalind Klein, Peggy
Organes; also featured were Paul Goldstein and Assistant Conductor Judy Geller.
Cantor Marton and his wife, Pearl
On December 2,1981, Cantor Marton was presented with the Lion of Judah
Award in recognition of a lifetime of dedicated and devoted service to the
Jewish people and all good causes to benefit the people of Israel.
Cantor Marton was given this tribute at an Israel Bonds Dinner on behalf of
the State of Israel Bonds.

Cemetery Committee of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center
The Cemetery Committee provides a very necessary function of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It is very important that the
Cemetery grounds are well kept and provide a peaceful resting place for our loved ones.
Our Cemetery Committee is chaired by Michael Schneider. Serving on the committee are Max Becker, Hymie Selber, Alan
Taffet, Dr. Joe Witten, Dr. Sam Witten, Jack Bettman, Joel Bressler, Nathan Sandler, Jack Becker and Joe Becker.
Mr. Kenneth Á. Bowden, Controller of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, also serves as general manager of our Cemetery. It is
his responsibility to oversee the upkeep and maintenance of the grounds. He has an excellent working relationship with Mr.
Jennewine who is general manager of Evergreen Cemetery. Mr. Jennewine has been very generous with his time and his staff,
Mr. Campbell, Mr. Miller and Mrs. Phillips. They have all taken excellent care of the Centers property, above and beyond what
is expected. We appreciate everything they do.
Johnny B. Mercer has been custodian of our Cemetery for over 20 years. Mr. Bergerson of Southern Monument Co., has
always been extremely helpful to us, too. We are very grateful to all these people who have given so generously of their time.

and friends in Jacksonville

Cub Scout Pack 14
Den 1, 2 & 3 worked and played weekly in many activities that helped them move thru the
levels of scouting . . . Besides achievments many friendships were developed and a feeling of
brotherhood was created when the groups got together.
The annual Pinewood Derby was a huge success. The competition was intense and everyone
followed the cub scout motto: “Do your best.” Inclement weather did not impede the fun at a
spring park meeting. The boys made their cane poles, used them to catch many fish, and
participated in a canoeing activity. Honors, advancements and promotions were awarded at the
traditional Blue & Gold Banquet. The atmosphere was created with decorations made by the
boys. The final acitivity - an overnight - was super fun for scouts and parents alike.
Many of the boys are looking forward to more exciting scouting adventures in 5743.
— Lorraine Jenkins
Den 3 (Weeblo): Sean Ussof,
Jeffrey Ghelerter, Michael Schultz,
Jonathan Goldberg and Den
Leader, Stephen Ghelerter.
Den 1: Michael Miller, Kyle Jenkins, Michael Flashen, Josh
Nathanson, David Bielski, Andy Alterman, Shane Steinfeld, Jay
Becker, Jay Weinstein and Den Mother Lorraine Jenkins.
Den 2: Jeffrey Myers, Aaron Kunsberg, David Schnipper, Alex
Greenbaum, Seth Rothstein and Den Mother Linda Kunsberg.
Boy Scout Troop 14
Boy Scout Troop 14 sponsored by the Jacksonville Jewish Center enjoyed an active
year in 1981-82. The troop program included outdoor camping and a variety of other
activities as varied as the interests of the troop members.
Troop 14 hosted its first Super Bowl of Scouting in 1982. The overnight camping
format for the Super Bowl included an array of competitive events in scouting skills and
games between our Troop 14 and Troop 12 of Temple Ahavath Chesed. A sampling of
the events included an evening “brain brawl-, soccer shootout, knot-tying rescue relay,
and a blindfolded compass course.
The Center troop played host to the Jacksonville Tea Men who performed a soccer
mini clinic for the scouts. The Tea Men, Dennis Witt, George Berrios and Ringo Cantillo,
thrilled the Scouts with trick shots and demonstrations of soccer skills with the Scouts
actively participating.
Troop 14 earned money for the purchase of badly needed bullet-proof vests for the
Jacksonville Sheriff’s Office.
Troop 14 earned one of five blue ribbons awarded at the first annual River Bend
District Camporee at Camp Baden Powell. Scouts combined the enlightening and
beautiful St. Augustine Historic Trail Hike with first aid classes on the beach of Anastasia
Island. Troop 14 also attended Scout World at the Jacksonville Naval Air Station where the boys enjoyed camping, scouting exhibitions, hot
air balloon liftoffs, swimming and fun along with baseball great, Ted Williams. Scout Andy Morrison led the troop in the sale of Scout World
tickets.
Scouts Sean Usoff and Jeff Ghelerter enjoyed a week at scout summer camp increasing their scouting and leadership skills. The annual Blue
and Gold Banquet was highlighted by skits presented by the troop members that received a PG rating from the delighted audience. Members
of Troop 14 participated admirably leading services for another memorable Scout Sabbath.
Congratulations go to Assistant Scoutmaster, Bill Wilensky, for successfully completing the first phase of the advanced Wood Badge
Leadership Training Course.
An even better year for Troop 14 is expected in 1982-83 with the leadership of new troop committee chairman, Steven Ghelerter. Boy Scout
Troop 14 is for all boys ages 11 through 17. Boys interested in joining Troop 14 should call the Center office.
Scoutmaster: Randy Silverberg, Asst. Scoutmaster: Billy Wilensky - Todd Berman, Steven Broward, Steve Chamblin, Jeffrey Ghelerter, Brad Giddens, John
Ingwersen, David Kagan, David Klein, Matt Kulchin, David Lazarus, Kevin McShea, Robert Moore, Andy Morrison, Roy Pomeranz, Scott Sanders, Roy Smith,
Jr. Roy Sucholeiki and Sean Usoff.

The Mr. & Mrs. Club. Formed in 1953 as an affiliate of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center. Meets on the third Saturday of each month for an evening of dancing to
a live band, dinner and entertainment. Ends the year with a New Years Eve
Gala providing professional entertainment.

Israel Kaplan Lodge #800 B’NAI B’RITH is an active organization in the Jewish
Community of Jacksonville. The lodge meets monthly with general meetings and
has dinners several times a year. Lodge membership is at the 275 mark for this
year. Various projects are held during the year to raise funds for B’NAI B’RITH
youth services. Hillel Foundations at the various state universities are supported
by B’NAI B’RITH as well as local A.Z.A. Chapters and B.B.G. Chapters. The local
lodge under the direction of Milton Hecht raised funds during the year 1979 and
purchased a torah for the Hillel Foundation at Florida State University in
Tallahassee. Every December lodge members gather to ring the bell for the
Salvation Army in downtown Jacksonville. Any member of the Jewish Community
interested in joining B’NAI B’RITH should contact the lodge president, Stuart
Hecht at 731-3406 for further information.
Stuart I. Hecht
PRESIDENT

During the coming year the Federation will be moving
into its new office building on Old St. Augustine Road. Our
Community Services will expand considerably, particularly
in the areas of family life education. These programs will be
provided in a variety of formats working with and through
the four congregations, River Garden and Jewish Family &
Children’s Services. We will also expand our Leadership
Development efforts so that future leadership will be
cultivated and available when needed.
The Federation will continue to conduct the Annual
Combined Jewish Appeal which raises monies for our local
agencies as well as the United Jewish Appeal and national
organizations. The Federation has made major increases in
its commitment to both our local Jewish Family &
Children’s Services and the River Garden Hebrew Home
for the Aged. Our Russian Resettlement program continues
to be a model program throughout the southeast part of the
United States. Federation programs will continue to
provide services in areas such as Senior Citizen
programming, Single Parent Family programming, College
Age programs, Jewish Singles in their 20’s, 30’s and 40’s,
etc.
The Federation provides a vehicle for service to our
community and it is the hope of the Officers and Board that
we unify our Jewish community for the betterment of all
individuals* and organizations.

Henry Kramer Library & Resource Center
Chairman - Minnie Schreiber
Tofield Collection
Co-Chairmen: Diane Fages and May Goldie Stillman
Belle Gendzier
Solomon Schechter Day School Library
Co-Chairmen of Mothers: Lauren Rothstein
Sharon Witten
Carol Schneider
Marlene Bossen
Ginger Proctor
Library Cart
Co-Chairman: Lillian Meizlik
Rita Gendzier Judaica Collection
Co-Chairmen: Tobi Meisel
Florence Schreiber The Solomon Schechter Library plays an important role in the Day School
Hermine Newman program.
Treasurer: Roselyn Selber
Our attractive library has been beautifully decorated. It has made tremendous
progress since its modest beginning in 1955, and has been responsible for many
programs.
The Library Sisterhood Shabbat sponsored a library program with a book review by
Rose Entman. Tobi Meisel told about magazines and periodicals available for
information as well as pleasurable reading. The Library Cart was present on this
occasion for checking out books and periodicals.
The Library Cart is available every fourth Saturday of the month after services.
This encourages Center members to enjoy reading books and periodicals.
The volunteers from the Solomon Schechter PTA kept the Solomon Schechter Day
School Library open two days a week during the school term until we obtained the ser¬
vices of a splendid librarian Mrs. Camille Kenny who taught library skills to the stu¬
dents. The Solomon Schechter Day School Library resources have grown. This plays
an important role in the Day School program.
The Tofield Collection has grown. Many fine volumes of talmudic literature,
volumes on Jewish life, Zionism, humor and fiction have been added to the collection.
Recently the Library received a donation of twenty tapes dealing with a variety of
subjects pertaining to Jewish life and community. These tapes are available for
discussion groups, classes and meeting programs.
The Rita Gendzier Judaica Collection is studying additions for this meaningful
display.
Library committee volunteers devote many service hours necessary for the
administration of this important facility. The Library is grateful for the generous The Rita Gendzier Judaica Collection - adds
support of the Center Membership. The many member contributions are used to a beautiful touch to our Library,
purchase new books and library supplies.

SURVIVAL WEEKEND
On May 8 and 9, Rabbi Dov Kentof and twelve teen-agers and adults traveled to Fernandina Beach to spend a challenging
weekend in the wilderness. With the co-operation of Project S.S.E.P. -Outward Bound Program, they spent the weekend
striving to reinforce! the concept of success and personal achievement while participating in a grueling weekend of obstacle
courses. The pictures shown clearly show the strain and concentration involved in the maneuvers.

Mount Carmel Gardens
Officers - 1982-83
President Mary Foor
1st Vice President Buddy Woods
2nd Vice President Eunice Safer
Treasurer Israel Schemer
Recording Secretary Dorothy Levine
Corresponding Secretary Pauline Schemer
Almost everyone in Jacksonville knows about Mt. Carmel and its importance as a Senior Citizen complex in our town.
Together with the Kosher Nutrition Site, located here, it has become well-known throughout our city, and is among the first
places where older folks apply when seeking a new home and an easier way of life.
It has been a busy year for all at Mount Carmel. Individually and collectively, we’ve been deeply involved with the many
projects offered, in educational courses, as well as volunteer work in our building and in our community. The improvements here
include a new roof; our lawn has been landscaped, beautifying the front of our building; cable television has been installed; and
many safety devices are now part of our daily living.
We have become well known, via television, newspaper and word-of-mouth, as very important for our social, entertaining, and
many other activities. Politically, our Mary Foor was “co-Mayor” for the city of Jacksonville for a day, as part of the Mayor’s
Older Buddies in Goverment Day - and rated a lovely article in the Times Union, including a picture with the Mayor. Mitzi
Shumer also spent the day, with Nancy Crabb, Council person for District 4, as MOB representative for Government Day, and
had a wonderful time meeting and mingling with all the dignitaries. At the Mayor’s May Day party, Fannie Kaufman was again
selected as “Queen of the May”, and was rewarded with her crown, a beautiful bouquet and a lovely plaque.
Our Mt. Carmel Entertainers and Mt. Carmel Singers are still performing whenever and wherever they are asked. They are
always called on whenever the Mayor has an affair for its Senior citizens, and for the third consecutive year have put on their
show at the Mayor’s Fish-a-Thon, before over a thousand people. They ahve been cited on the R.S.V.P. honor roll for
exceptionals -- and have received a certificate to that effect.
This year we celebrated our tenth anniversary, with a party to which the entire Jewish community was invited. This included
speeches by important personages, food, drink, and dancing to a live band. It was indeed a gala affair, and one which will be long
remembered.
We have in our building a large group of dedicated people, friendly and happy - enjoying their home here in Mount Carmel.

Adult Education
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Adult Education program is designed
to offer the members of our community the opportunity to expand their
knowledge of our history, religion and culture. The program continues to
attract hundred of people from our community who want to engage in a
program of Jewish Study on a variety of levels. The Adult Education
courses include: Jewish philosophy, the Bible, Jewish synagogue and
home skills, Haftorah and Torah chanting, and a Bat Mitzvah program for
women.
The HEBREW LITERACY CAMPAIGN is based on the unique
feature of making classes available day, morning and evening.
Professional and skilled lay people instruct the classes in beginners and
intermediate Hebrew.
This year’s SCHOLAR-IN-RESIDENCE was Jerusalem Post
correspondent, Wolf Blitzer. The MINYANAIRE is an ongoing Sunday
morning program combining prayer, breakfast and a discussion and
lecture by local authorities on a vast range of topics.
HAVUROT of fellowships of groups, meet socially, within the intimacy
of individual homes for the purpose of study, discussion and celebration of
Jewish life. If you are interested, please contact Rabbi David Gaffney.
THE
Jy ADULT
STUDY
INSTITUTE
Sisterhood Bat Mitzvah Class
Minyanaire
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Minyanaire program is for men and women of all ages and lifestyles. Each program begins with
services which are held in the intimate atmosphere of the Witten Chapel. The Minyanaire program, which is usually held on
Sunday mornings, features speakers on a variety of subjects. A breakfast is served and is a pleasant change of pace from the
usual morning routine.
This year Evan Yegelwel was responsible for the excellent programs presented at the Minyanaire. He was ably assisted by
Barry Minkoff, Bill Goldberg and Marty Rosenberg.
Plans are being made for the coming year. Volunteers are needed so this program can continue. Please contact the Center
office if you would like to be a part of this vital and exciting program.

The Jacksonville District of the Zionist Organization of
America has many activities, including education about, the
promotion of, and public relations for the State of Israel. Our
national organization is one of the most effective advocates for
Israel because of our constituency or membership and
traditionally has always had clout where it counts in the
government and the mass media.

husband Sidney Entman.

trees in Israel this year in memory of Sidney Entman. In addition, we once again co-sponsored with the Jacksonville Jewish
Center a weekend program by Wolf Blitzer, the ever popular Washington correspondent of the Jerusalem Post. We have
several innovative ideas for programs in the coming year.

===== PAGE 76 =====
Hadassah
Hadassah, the largest volunteer women’s organization, consists of a membership of 370,000, dedicated to medical research
and in aiding Israel’s immigrants to rehabilitate themselves. It is the second largest employer in Israel.
This year Hadassah celebrates it’s 70th anniversary, carrying out the work begun by its founder, Henrietta Szold. The
Jacksonville Chapter of Hadassah, consists of three groups: Tikva, which meets during the day every second Tuesday of the
month, September through May; Hannah Senesch meets on the second Wednesday evening, and Shir-Li, our youngest group,
meets every first Monday evening.
The three groups each plan their own activities of fund-raising and education, co-operating with the other groups, so as to
reach the goals which National Hadassah sets for the Chapter.
The funds raised by these groups support the Hadassah Hebrew University Medical Center, Mt. Scopus Hospital, Hadassah
Medical organization, Youth Aliyah, Hadassah Israel Education Services, Jewish National Fund, Zionist Youth Activities and
Camps here in the United States, for youngsters desiring to live a Jewish experience, and to study in Israel during the summer
months.
Anyone interested in learning more about Hadassah is welcome to call one of the members listed. There is a group for
everyone, and we welcome your call.
On this New Year, we wish for you and yours, a year of health and Happiness. L’Shona Tov!

Why does a Conservative synagogue support and promote Camp Ramah?
Camp Ramah provides the opportunity to offer a total Jewish living experience for children and teenagers in the relaxed and
enjoyable atmosphere of a summer camp. Values built on shared experience and emotion reach our sons and daughters in a
manner impossible in a formal school program. Over the years, Ramah has helped instill a deeper commitment to Judaism in
many of its participants.
The Center believes that benefits accrue to the congregation, not just to the individual. We have therefore made monies
available to reduce the financial cost for qualified students regardless of need. These monies are not part of the regular Center
budget, but rather are raised by donations to the Myra Thier Lazarus Ramah Fund, through Sisterhood, and from other sources.
Two families have helped us greatly. The Gordon family has established a scholarship fund in memory of the beloved Robert J.
Gordon. A long list of deserving boys and girls have been able to go to Ramah because of this scholarship.
Abe Selber established in his will a perpetual trust for specific Jewish educational purposes. With the full support of his
children, Iris and Franklin, who have never lost their interest in the Center, the proceeds of this trust have also been used to send
campers to Ramah.
It is our hope that the Camp Ramah experience will continue to be a valuable complement to a formal Jewish education.
The following attended Camp Ramah this summer:
Melissa Roey, Manya and David Lazarus, Reuben Bressler, Coleman Brodsky, Laurie and Beth Greenburg, Marcy Kesler,
Simeon Abramson, Dennis Mizrahi, Katrin Echt, Cheryl Bossen and Steven Shapiro.
Janet Jacobson attended the Ramah Israel Seminar.
U.S.Y. on Wheels is not just another tour of North
America. It is a total experience of intensive Jewish
living and educational and social programming within
the United Synagogue Youth. Classes in Judaica
directly related to the experiences of the trip are held
every day and are supplemented by special interest
seminars. The WHEELS itineraries visit the most
interesting, exciting, and diverse attractions and
natural sights on this continent. The plan has been
prepared in careful consultation with experienced
travel authorities including USYers and advisors who
have previously participated on WHEELS.
Any USY member between the ages of 14 and 18
who will have completed the 9th grade by June 1983,
may apply. Registration is given to those whose
organizational and educational background indicate
they will benefit most. All USYers are encouraged to
apply. Stephanie Gray was lucky enough to attend.

===== PAGE 84 =====
Message from the President
We are approaching the 80th anniversary of the founding of our
synagogue. The years ahead should be as exciting as those in the past.
The Center is moving forward to meet the rapidly changing conditions of
our lives.
I believe the members of the early years of the synagogue would be
amazed at our present day activities. We continue to follow a program of
traditional Judiaism, but still incorporate contemporary features. Every
Jewish festival and holiday, without exception, is fully observed. Few cities
with as small a Jewish population as Jacksonville continue to have a daily
minyan evening, morning and noon. It is fantastic to realize that
substantially over 100 different individuals each week participate
in daily service. Our Shabbat service regularly has a minimum of 200 in
attendance. We are truly an observant synagogue.
We also care for the future generation. Our day school is second to
none in this city, public or private. We have over 200 children from 2 years
old through the seventh grade and an excellent and well attended
afternoon Hebrew School, Sunday School and High School.
There is no segment of the membership that is not provided with Jewish related activities. Going through this Year Book best
illustrates membership participation in all of these functions.
We are truly a “Center” for Jewish living in Jacksonville. We are most proud of our volunteer workers as well as the
professional staff. Needless to say, without them there would be no Center.
The years ahead require more of our membership to partake of the religious services as well as the educational and social
programs. We must have this to be certain that our children and their children will have a Center. As of today our synagogue is in
a superb position to help meet the challenges of Jewish living. We must have your help.
L’ Shanah Tovah Tikatevv
Sol H. Proctor

Carolyn Krestul
NATIONALBBPCOUNCIL OF JEWISH WOMEN
EDUCATION SOCIAL ACTION SERVICE
President Carolyn Krestul
Vice Presidents Dottie Shlafer
Beverly Horowitz
Lois Schlesinger
Joy Korman
Corresponding Secretary LoisChepenik

Treasurer Beth Shorstein
The National Council of Jewish Women, the oldest women’s volunteer
organization in the United States, is dedicated, in the spirit of Judaism, to advancing
human welfare and the democratic way of life. Through a coordinated program of
education, service, advocacy and social action, NCJW works in the Jewish and
general communities, locally, nationally, and internationally.
NCJW’s priorities include issues concerning Women, Children and Youth, the Aging, Israel and Jewish Life.
The Jacksonville Section of the NCJW is currently involved in projects that include an annual Mental Health Forum, co-sponsored with the
MENTAL Health Association and JFC; Pre-school Vision Screening, and the Art Enrichment Program (“Picture Lady”) through which
volunteers are trained by the Jacksonville Art Museum to introduce art to students in both public and private schools.
With a grant allocated by the National office, the Jacksonville Section organized the CASA (Court Appointed Special Advocate) program in
our community. This program trains volunteers to act as a “friend of the court” in the best interest of an abused or neglected child. This project
is currently funded by the State of Florida and, in accordange with Florida law, is called the Guardian Ad Litem program.
NCJW’s most recent effort, a Senior Citizen’s Day Camp program held a the Jacksonville Jewish Center and co-sponsored with the
Jacksonville Jewish Federation, was enjoyed by many of our communities “Seniors.”
The Jacksonville Section is presently participating in a new national project, a survey of adolescent girls in the juvenile justice system.
The major thrust of NCJW’s activities in Israel has been in education and social welfare, in a number of projects to aid in the development of
Israel’s most precious resource, its children. The Research Institute for Innovation in Education is one of NCJW’s program sin Israel; Ship-a-
box, another.
NCJW seeks members within the Jewish community of all ages and interests. An EVENING BRANCH and a COUNCILETTES group for
Jacksonville’s teens are currently a part of NCJW’s plans for expansion.
We invite you to join us!

Youth Banquet
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Annual Youth Banquet took place May 23,1982. U.S.Y., Kadima, Chalutzim, Boy Scouts,
Girl Scouts, Brownies and Cub Scouts and Leaders all participated in the evening’s program. Awards were given and the new
officers were installed. A delightful talent show concluded the evening which was co-ordinated by Carol Freedman.

A Scribe Visits
“The special calligraphy of the Torah has a spiritual quality uniquely Jewish, since it cannot be influenced by
changing secular esthetic influences.”
Alain Kirilli, artist
Rabbi Turkeltaub, an authentic Scribe, or sofer, came to the Jacksonville Jewish Center for the express purpose of examining
and repairing our Torah scrolls that are used for our Torah reading services. Members brought mezeuzot, that needed to
be examined and repaired; tefillin with frayed threads or knots too large or too small were also repaired by Rabbi Turkeltaub.
Children of the Day School were fascinated as they watched the scribe repair our Torah scrolls.
Sclihot Program
A special exciting Pre-Selihot program featured two dramatic presentations; “If Not Higher” by Y.L. Peretz and vignettes, “They
Shall Mount Up With Wings Like Eagles.” Members of the Center U.S.Y. were ably directed by Sheila Jacobson.

===== PAGE 105 =====
A Message From
Rabbi Dov Kentof
Director of
Education and Youth Director
We all want our children to have every opportunity
and advantage we may have missed. It’s a universal
human emotion, as old as Adam - the individual and
family-size version of the world wide human striving for
security and advancement - wanting our tomorrows to
be brighter than our yesterdays.
In planning to give your children all the economic,
social and educational advantages your means will allow
(and sometimes even beyond your means) are you
remembering that your children are Jewish?
What will this fact mean to your children - the fact that they are Jewish? Will it be a word to be
shouted at them in the streets? Will it be a burden, a source of conflict, confusion and
unhappiness? Will they be culturally orphaned, wandering about the fact of the earth rootless and
unrelated?
Or will their Jewishness be a source of strength and emotional security, giving your children
firm emotional roots in the wisdom, morality and beauty created by the Jewish people over a
span of three thousand years?
This advantage of having a foundation for their lives as American Jews - which you have missed
in your own life - is something you can provide your children by giving them a modern, effective
Jewish education, which will relate their spiritual and cultural heritage to the world of today. And
let’s remember that insecurity is no respect of age or sex. It starts with the very young, and it
affects boys and girls alike.
Here at the Jacksonville Jewish Center, we are very fortunate to have a culmination of great
facilities and an aggressive program. Young and old alike can experience Judaism in a most posi¬
tive form. Here, learning can be meaningful through Shabbat experience, camping, socialization,
conventions, friendship and much more. We invite the entire congregation to partake in what
the Center has to offer.
You can help your children to develop their own inner strength and emotional security ... it is
in your hands.
Let me greet you and your family with “a Happy New Year.”
Rabbi Dov Kentof.
Dov loves kids and kids love Dov

Consecration Classes
The first grade children and new students of the Solomon Schechter Day School along with the Alef Class of the Afternoon
Hebrew School were consecrated in a ceremony at the Jacksonville Jewish Center on Saturday morning, February 26,1982.
The ceremony marked the beginning of the children’s formal Hebrew and Judaic education and is a very meaningful event. Each
child received a certificate, miniature Torah and a traditional jar of honey. The children who were consecrated:
DAY SCHOOL: Leslie Adler, Jason Blume, Melissa Brodsky, Mark dayman, Brian Davis, Dana Davis, Lorien Friedlin, Aron Greenburg, Emma Greenwood,
Lee Kaplan, Paige Kornblum, Joni Press, Eduardo Romero, Havi Safer, Jennifer Sager, Ari Silverman, Andy Ussach, Irene Vavulitsky and Jonathan Witten.
AFTERNOON HEBREW SCHOOL: Valerie Baruch, Jill Ghelerter, Carol Ann Hall, Robert Hyken, Judith Jacobson, Melissa Kirshenbaum, Laurie Paul,
Jennie Schwab, Rachel Thaler and Julie Snitzer.

The Jewish Center’s Recreation Department’s goals are to provide the Jewish community
with programs and activities that promote the improvement of physical skills, health, the
development of special interest and/or hobbies, and to provide the opportunity for relaxation
and social camaraderie.
Many of the recreation activities take place on the Center Campsite which consists of
approximately 10 acres of beautifully wooded campgrounds, complete with an olympic-size
swimming pool, bath houses, tennis courts, softball fields, and outdoor basketball court,
badminton area, children’s playground, gazebo, snack bar and shaded picnic area.
Within the main building is a regulation basketball court, the fully-equipped Neal Portnoy
Youth Lounge and an arts and crafts room, a large room for dances and a versatile stage for
musical and dramatic productions and a meat and dairy kitchen with the most modern
equipment. We take pride in recreation program and the marvelous facilities of our Center.
Recreation Programs
Sunday Sports Association
Sunday Funday
Winter Funtime (Holiday break recreation, games crafts,
sports and trips)
Learn to Swim
Family Recreation (Summer Pool and Nature Days)
Soccer Drop-In Program
Scouting Programs

===== PAGE 129 =====
Yammit
1. Through the reflections of the bus windows we
see the naked wasteland from which a city was
created.
- The Spirit
2. Apartment homes were built on beautiful
plazas.
In the beginning there was only the nothingness of barren sand as far as the eye
could see. And then they came -- a small group of Jews - with courage,
determination, perseverance, and the will to create for themselves a new life,
home, in this old desert - just as their ancestors had done generations ago.
Slowly, deliberately, steadfastly they worked, and strained and dug and built and
their dream became a reality. Out of sandy wasteland came a beautiful city. Parks
rang with the shouts and laughter of the children at play. The plazas were crowded
with people enjoying themselves by singing or playing music to entertain their
friends. Lush patches of green formed a pattern in the desert as the farmers worked
their magic to bring forth food from the earth. The shops were alive with activity as
the people admired and bought the goods and handiwork of the merchants and
craftsmen. And the homes were filled with joy and happiness and satisfaction as
families shared their Jewish heritage and took pride in their accomplishments. This
was truly the personification of the Jewish spirit.
Then with cruel swiftness it was over. This was no longer their land, their home.
It was decreed that this land be returned to Egypt. The dream became a nightmare.
The bulldozers came. And much more quickly than it was built, this beautiful city of
bricks and stone and mortar made from the sands of the barren desert was
changed to piles of rubble -- broken bricks and stones and mortar - which in time
will return again to its original form.
And in the end there was only the nothingness of barren sand as far as the eye
could see.
Bob Bossen
evidence that something existed here but soon
even it was gone and now .. a naked wasteland.
7. As our bus was leaving, we turned around, for
one last time, and looked at the city we would
never see again . . .

Yammit and bought the last ice cream cone from
the refreshment shop.
6. We visited the monument to all of the Israeli
soldiers who were killed in this area in the war of
1967.

Girl Scout Troop #162
The 1981-82 year for the Center Girl Scouts was just the greatest. Our leader’s name is Clara Mann and she cannot be beat.
This year on Scout Leaders Day we gave her a dish garden with a card to tell how much we need her and appreciate her. There
were about 18 girls in our troop this year and we worked on all kinds of badges. We received these badges at our last meeting for
this year.
Some of our activities were a camp-out trip to Silver Springs and Wild Waters, a swimming party at the Center pool, we
looked at stars through a telescope, and made a lot of fun things.
I think this year was just great. Thanks to Mrs. Mann. I also would like to thank Irene Mann and the mothers who helped the
troop.
Leaders: Clara Mann
Irene Mann
Jewel Ann Achord

Girl Scouting is more than a club, it is a nationwide, worldwide movement of girls ages 7-17. Girl Scouts make a
promise and live by the Girl Scout Laws. These simple guides prepare a young girl to live in our bewildering
modern world.
If you are interested in being a scout or a scout leader call Clara Mann 733-6472.
Brownie Troop #147
The Brownie Troop #147 of the Jacksonville Jewish Center will begin a new year with a wide variety of activities. Girls ages 7-9
are invited to join the troop. Gayle Thaler is the Browner leader. Please call her if you are interested in joining or helping the
troop. Weekly meetings take place at the Jacksonville Jewish Center.

Religious Services —- Traditional prayer services are held daily, morning and
evening in the Witten Chapel. Friday Family services, Sabbath and Holiday
Services are observed throughout the entire year.
Personal Religious Observances — Traditional Jewish customs are observed
in connection with Circumcision, Naming of Girls, Pidyon Ha-ben, Bar
Mitzvah, Bat Mitzvah, Confirmation, Marriages, Conversion to Judaism,
Bereavement.
Education — Daily Kindergarten and Nursery & Day Care with outstanding
program of secular and religious content. Hebrew school, carefully graded
with intensive Hebrew • content, including Jewish history and custpms,
Sunday School for kindergarten, first and second grades: Solomon Schechter
Day School, a graded secular and Hebrew School, 1st through 7th grades;
Hebrew High School with Pre-Jr. and Junior Congregations and Minyanaire.
Extension Services — Library, outstanding collection of juvenile and adult
Jewish books; Adult Education, religious and cultural Jewish courses; music
programs of religious and cultural Jewish music; P.T.A.; Sisterhood,
Ha’Rayim, a fellowship of young families; Center Couples Club, social
activities provided by Mr. and Mrs. Club, Single Adults; Family Recreation
Program (Olympic pool), summer week-days and Sundays for all ages.
Youth Activities — ATID for college age youth; United Synagogue Youth,
Kadima, Chalutzim, Boy Scouts, Cub Scouts, Girl Scouts, Brownies; Sunday
Funday; athletics, programs for youth and adults; Center Day Camp and
summer program at our 36 acre site
Family Recreation Program— Center Campsite . . . swimming, athletics,
snack bar; available for members during the summer months. Campsite
includes olympic-size swimming pool, 2 tennis courts, baseball, soccer and
football fields and playground.
For additional information, call the Center office — 268-6736

Sesame Street
On May 24, 1982 the Masada group
of the Solomon Schechter Day School
presented a Hebrew production of
“Sesame Street” to the entire school.
The success of the program was the
result of months of work on the part of
the children in the class and their
teacher, Edith Horovitz.
The cast included Larissa Zaulyanov
as Grover, Amy Funk and Laurie
Greenburg as Snuffulufagas, Jennifer
Verstandig as Big Bird, Jana Chepenik
as Bert, Allison Ginsburg as Ernie, Val
Teper as Mr. Hooper, Sean Gibson as
Kermit, Matthew Kulchin as Cookie
Monster, Steven Cantor as the Race
Car Driver, Cheryl Stone as the Little
girl, Jonathan Goldberg as the Train
Conductor and Coleman Brodsky as
Oscar.
Judy Reppert designed the stage and
props and Shirley Bielski was the
musical director and pianist.

===== PAGE 142 =====
The State of Israel presents
The Mediterranean - Dead Sea Canal Project
Israel announces its most ambitious economic project; the building of a Canal from the
Mediterranean to the Dead Sea for production of Hydro-Electric power.
The Canal will ultimately produce more than 20% of Israel’s total Energy needs and alleviate
to a larger extent the Import of oil which in 1980 cost 25 billion dollars.
As water cascades from the High ground on the Mediterranean to the Dead Sea the Canal will
provide Hydro-Electric power which by the year 2000 should produce 3,000 megawatts of
electricity out of a national total of 10,000 megawatts.
The Canal will provide solar ponds to soak up heat from the sun, make water available for
cooling future power stations.
The Canal will also create lakes for tourist attractions, agricultural projects and fisheries and
establish industrial and building enterprises.
The Canal project lifts the importance of Israel Bonds to a higher than ever level. While more
than 5 billion dollars in Israel Bonds has been sold world Jewry will quickly produce another
billion dollars to provide the funds for this historic project.
You can be part of that history.
The State of Israel Bond organization is the exclusive group, responsible for the raising of
$100 Million in 1981-82 as seed money for this project.
For additional information contact Dr. Nelson Goldman, Jacksonville chairman, or write Mr. Bert
Sales, State of Israel Bonds, Box 667, Palm Beach, Fla 33480.

===== PAGE 152 =====
SUNDAY SCHOOL
The Sunday School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is planned expressly for children in Kindergarten, First and Second
Grades. A two hour program provides each child the opportunity to experience the richness of their Jewish heritage through
song, dance, role playing, cooking, short stories, games arts and crafts. Emphasis is placed on the holidays and festivals. Jewish
values and mitzvot are encouraged.
The objectives of our Sunday School are as follows:
1. To provide the young child with the opportunity for wholesome Jewish experiences, especially those related to the
observance of Jewish festivals both at home and in the synagogue.
2. To make meaningful to the child the Jewish element in his environment.
3. To offer and provide opportunities for Jewish creative expression through handiwork, song poetry, prayer, rhythms and
music discussion, drama, etc.
4. To acquaint the child with Jewish folklore, particularly those stories which teach ethical principles anchor are related the
Jewish festivals.
5. To establish a foundation of knowledge of Jewish practices, history and thinking, as well as a basic Hebrew vocabulary
which can later be built upon and expanded in the Hebrew and Judaica High Schools.
Sunday School co-ordinator is Trida Bloom, Judy Geller is the music instructor.
The Sunday School Staff and students enjoy their final day at the Center Campsite Pool

Lawrence Rackow
Executive Director
In 1982 the Jewish Family and Children’s Services, Inc., the two man casework arm of the Jewish community, observes its sixty-
fifth anniversary, the thirtieth under the directorship of Lawrence Rackow and the twentieth under its current name.
Throughout its history, even as the United Jewish Charities and the Jewish Welfare Society, it has had three goals: to strengthen
and or restore family functioning and stability; to help individuals lead happier and healthier lives; and to enable individuals to
approach their maximum potential. In 1981,634 individuals from 527 families were helped in one or more of the four programs set
up to help reach these goals: Counselling, Senior Citizen, Emergency Financial Assistance, and Resettlement.
In its main program, Counselling, beside the basic forms found in most agencies, individual, marital, parent-child, physical illness,
and mental illness, and agency is also licensed to place children in foster care and for adoption. It is also payee or guardian for
incompetent persons, has a monthly outreach program at the State Hospital in Macclenny and at the prisons in Raiford, and
years ago it established a weekly group for isolated and dependent persons. In 1982, jointly with the Jewish Federation, it
established two series of Family Life Education. Nathaniel Greenwood, the Social Worker, was sent to a five day workshop on
Mediation to help sharpen and broaden our counseling services. 231 persons were served in 1981.
We Are So Delighted That So Many Of You Nice People Enjoy

Message from
We usher in the High Holy Days of this New Year, 5743, with
prayers for peace for Israel and all mankind. We do so in our
newly completed, beautiful sanctuary, enjoying the comfort of
the new seats and the aesthetic satisfactions provided by the high
quality of style and design of our new furnishings. The delay
in completing our synagogue interior only serves to highlight
the appreciation felt now that we have realized its completion.
I cannot overstate the sense of gratitude and the collective
thank you we need to offer the chairmen and members of
various committees for making these improvements possible.
We applaud Philip Selber and the Interior Design Committee for
the dedication they have shown over these many years. A
“yasher-koah” to Laurie DuBow, Leonard Setzer, Alan Gordon
and the members of the Building Fund Committee for their hard
work to make this enterprise financially feasible. We thank our
friends and devoted members who guaranteed the bank loan
and to many whose generosity compelled them to pledge their
support, again and again. We are very grateful to Nathan Krestul,
Chairman of the Board of the Center, for the years of dedication
in overseeing the innumerable details of each phase of the
design and to Buddy Shorstein whose steady hand and
administrative capabilities helped to bring us to this day. We
know that those mentioned above along with the many members of their committees who met and planned, deliberated
and finally resolved a program for beautifying our facility will know the fulfillment that comes from the
blessing of satisfaction that enables them now to enjoy the fruition of their labor.
Beyond comfort and aesthetics, the new sanctuary conveys a central and fundamental message. The crown of our new
synagogue is the Aron Kodesh, the Ark, designed by Ami Shamir. This unique and extraordinary Ark, is in fact, a sculpture
depicting the Biblical story of Jacob’s ladder. The Ark suggests that through prayer, the Jew, as Jacob, rises heavenward.
Through Torah, an expression of His love for His people, God descends to earth. The Torah, the source of the teaching
and guidance of Jewish history and tradition, is the means by which God makes His place among us. “V'nikdashti b’toh
b’nei yisrael” ... “I will be hallowed among the people of Israel.” (Lev. 22:32) Jacob’s ladder states that there is no
bifurcation world of God and the world of man. God needs us as His co-partners to complete and repair an imperfect
world. Man needs God for meaning and purpose. Jacob's ladder conveys the central message that heaven and earth meet
in the mind, heart and soul of man ... in his willingness to serve, to consecrate, to heal, to comfort and to repair.
The Ark is visibly decorated with stylized graphics that quote central and Biblical passages that speak to our tradition,
our faith and our belief. What endures beyond time and substance is the revelation of "the word,” “the teaching,” and
“the idea.” Although man is not immortal, his God inspired ideas and wisdom endure forever. The great shrines of Jewish
life were never embodied in physical structures but in these words ... the Ten Commandments, the prophecies of an
Isaiah, the quest for justice of an Amos, the teaching of Akiba, the gentleness and compassion of the Baal Shem Tov.
Wherever Jews have lived, Judaea,... Babylonia ... Spain ... Poland ... Israel and the United States, they have left the
legacy of “the word” and “the teaching” which will endure.
The Ark, as Jacob’s ladder, reminds us of a vivid dream that Jacob had and his consecration of the place in which he
found himself as his Beth El... the House of God. This is what a sanctuary is. It becomes a House of God when it sustains us
with the vision of what we stand for and when it commits us to high principles and lofty purposes and when it raises us
beyond the confining ceilings we have placed over our heads.
The sanctuary becomes a Beth El when it provides us with a direction with which to lead our lives so that we remain
neither aimless wanderers nor bored by a life devoid of purpose and meaning. A sanctuary becomes a Beth El, a House of
God, when it helps us to weather the storms we inevitably find in life and when we create the fellowship of concern and
care; a congregation bound by compassion and sensitivity.
A vision and purpose, a direction and goal, a setting of compassion and healing,... these are beyond what furnishings
can provide. A true sanctuary cannot be ordered. It has to be created. It has to be nurtured by our own designs, what we
are willing to create and provide with our hearts and hands.
As we begin the Rosh Hashanah of 5743 with the traditional blessing “ ... Who has kept us in life, preserved us and
enabled us to reach this season,” may we dedicate ourselves to make of our synagogue a sanctuary, a Beth El, a ladder
joining heaven and earth.
Inge and I and the members of our family wish you and yours a year of health, happiness, purpose, blessing and peace.
AMEN
Rabbi David Gaffney
the Rabbi
Rabbi & Inge Gaffney, Mickey & Shalva Schlisser & Asher Gaffney.

Solomon Schechter Day School
The continuing growth of the Day School attests to
the fulfillment of the dreams of the founders in 1960. The
Day School has grown to a record 206 enrollment, from
Jumping Jacks (2 years old) through the 7th grade.
The Solomon Schechter Day School was founded
with the premise that our children will, as they mature,
continue the heritage of our people, support Israel,
participate in Jewish communal activities, and assume
responsibilities of leadership, thus ensuring the quality of
Jewish life and the future of our community.
In addition to a rich program of Hebrew and Judaic studies, we must provide a superior secular
studies program. Our common goal has always been an exceptional educational institution for
Judaic and Secular studies. Our dream has come true. Our school is open to all Jewish children
in the community regardless of affiliation or ability to pay.
There is overwhelming evidence that the students of Jewish day schools remain committed to
the survival of Jewish life and provide the reservoir of leadership needed for a strong Jewish
community.
Marilyn Sandler, Principal
Evelyn Borstein
Day School Secretary
Laura Edwards

Day Camp 1982
Where everyday is an adventure
Camping can be one of the most meaningful experiences
a child will ever have. Our Camp offers not, only a
situation in which children can learn and develop by
interacting with other children, but it offers a full scope of
activities designed to make a child aware of our Jewish
heritage, to develop new friendships, enjoy the wonders
of nature that may be found on pur large wooded
campsite and the importance of active sports.

Chalutzim
GENERAL AIM: Jewish families today look to the synagogue as the center for Jewish activity: religious, education, social
and recreational. A major goal of the synagogue and its school is the education of youth with a firm base of knowledge, Jewish
identification of youth, a sense of pride in their heritage, and a commitment to Judaism. The goal of Chalutzim is to bring about
the internalization of Jewish values, attitudes and behavior patterns by supplementing the child’s formal and religious
education with informal Jewish learning experience.
Officers
(Advisors: Felice Shriftman & Randee Steinberg)
President David Silverman
Vice President Steve Cantor
Vice President/Social Worker Evan Ageloff
Secretary Lara Shriftman
Treasurer Lee Pollock
Member-At-Large Jenny Verstandig
Advisors Felice Shriftman and Randee Steinberg get help from Anne
DePaul.
Annetta Kornblum helps Jenny Verstandig and David Silverman make
Hamantaschen.
Objectives
1. To recognize the importance of Shabbat and holiday
observance.
2. To recognize the need for regular devotion both
individually and in groups.
3. To develop an appreciation and willingness to work for
the synagogue.
4. To increase the use of Hebrew in informal settings.
5. To establish a communal sense by supporting community
and civic activities.
6. To recognize the importance of Israel as a modern center
for world Jewry.
7. To develop a Jewish identity through music and dance.
8. To develop an appreciation of Jewish life.
Chalutzim go bowling, L-R Marty Gottleib, Kate Freedman, Craig
Kornblum, Leon Jackler.

Hebrew High School
The Judaica High School is the creation of the synagogue to offer Jewish youth an opportunity to explore the broad expanse
of resources available through our heritage. This program seeks to provide exciting, innnovative exploration of Judaism upon
which each student might build. It involved children in 8th through 12th grades and is required for Confirmation.

The Symbolism of Israel
Random Impressions of an Inspiring Journey,
Bob and Marlene Bossen
Peaceful co-existence! Here at the “Good Fence”
on the Lebanese border, and Arab leaves the
Israeli clinic after being treated by an Israeli
doctor! People who need people can and will live
in peace.
On a peaceful, productive kibbutz where people
go about their daily labor and children laugh and
play, this bunker is a constant reminder of the
ever present dangers.
These young Israeli soldiers, male and female, are
hitching rides to be home in time for Shabbat.
Even their ever-present machine guns don’t keep
people from picking them up.
Inside the 2,000 year old walled city of Jerusalem,
our emotions are stirred as we retrace the steps
and try to visualize the lives of our ancestors.
Excavations continue to reveal our glorious
heritage.
The Knesset where the Israeli Parliament meets.
It is said that there are as many differences of
opinion inside the Knesset as there are windows
on the outside.
Lest we Forget! Everywhere we went there was
the ever-present contrast of the carefree tourists
and the military vehicle with loaded guns
prepared for any eventuality.
It’s the thought that counts! In old synagogues we
visited there were arks of hand carved wood and
simple hand woven curtains. Each ark was
strikingly beautiful - because of the love and
reverence with which it was built.
This picture, to me, represents the whole idea of
Israel. The enduring strength and resolve of the
Jewish people are exemplified by the ancient and
massive stones of the Western Wall. The Jewish
ideals of living in peace and thanking God for all
blessings are demonstrated by men praying at the
wall. Life would be so simple if many would only
follow ten simple rules!
Against the backdrop of nature’s majestic beauty
stands a grim reminder of the Holocaust. A
sculpture of emaciated bodies wrapped in barbed
wire.

The Progressive Credit Union was organized in 1939 when a small group of businessmen formed the Jewish Progressive
Society to provide financial service to deserving persons of the Jewish faith. The group believed the cooperative movement
would relieve the financial distress brought on by the depression.
The Credit Union makes loans for family, personal or business needs. The interest rate charged is lower than the interest rate
of most lending institutions in the Jacksonville area. Savings deposits are guaranteed up to $100,000.00 by the Florida Credit
Union Guaranty Corporation. Life Savings Insurance insures the life of each individual member in an amount equal to his or her
savings and Loan Protection Insurance covers the life of each insurable borrower in the amount of the unpaid balance of his loan.
This insurance is available at no extra charge to members who qualify.
Recently the Progressive Credit Union honored several members for their dedication and meritorius service. Mr. Moe B.
Safer was chosen to become the first Chairman of the Board. Edwin Presser was selected to be the new president.
Special merit citations and plaques for outstanding service were presented to Mac Presser, Credit Committee Chairman
Emeritus and Eugene Henry, Credit Committee Member Emeritus. All officers and directors of this important community
project volunteer their services.
The Progressive Credit Union extends an invitation for all to join. Information may be obtained from any of the officers or
directors. The Progressive Credit Union office is located in the Florida National Bank Building, Room 759, phone 354-4770.
Jewish War Veterans
LT. MEYER LIEBOVITZ POST 199 Jacksonville, Florida
■ JWV is more than a veterans organization. More than a
Jewish organization. It is an amalgamation of Americans of
Jewish faith who share the common experience of having
served their country in time of war.
■ JWV was founded in 1896 to counteract slurs against
Jewish patriotism. Since then, it has been in the forefront of
the battle against anti-Semitism, bigotry and prejudice. In
upholding American democratic traditions, JWV fights
injustice and discrimination of all kinds.
■ JWV contributes greatly to the growth of a sympathetic
understanding of Israel and its problems among all
Americans. It is outspoken on issues that are affecting
permanent peace in the Middle East. Likewise, its
leadership role continues to help arouse American public
opinion against Soviet Union's anti-Jewish policies.
For Information: Acting Commander: Hyman Magil
Quartermaster: Meyer Caplan, 744-2607
■ JWV’s views are well known to Congress on such diverse
subjects as foreign policy, civil rights, defense spending,
veterans benefits, housing and education.
■ JWV, through its hospital, rehabilitation and veterans
service programs, assists the veteran and his dependents in
many ways. It maintains veteran service offices, manned by
professional experts, in major cities throughout the
country.
■ JWV, through its child welfare program, supports the Boy
Scout organization, provides summer camp scholarships
for underprivileged children, sponsors athletic league
tournaments. Its program includes sponsorship of
brotherhood rallies and the undertaking of civic betterment
projects in local communities.

Herman Paul
President
The River Garden Home has been a vital, integral part of the Jacksonville Jewish Cofnmunity for 36 years. There are very few communities fortunate
enough to have a geriatric care and rehabilitation center that has the capacity and resources to provide for 100% of the needs of the local Jewish population.
The primary mission of River Garden is to give long term care and short term rehabilitative care to older people who need the intensity of service, therapy and
support available in a residential setting and an environment supportive of Jewish identity. In addition, River Garden provides respite care, Hospice care,
geriatric assessment and counseling, and is a social service resource to the entire community.
River Garden serves the frail and ill aged. It stresses the “wellness” of the individual. River Garden attempts to compensate for the individual’s deficits
through its medical, nursing and psychosocial services and attempts to motivate the individual to utilize his postive assets to the fullest extent possible.
Through individualized plans of care, the Home tries to strike a living balance between institutional requirements and individual needs and styles. This positive
accent on living, with a variety of social, cultural and recreational programs helps to create the special climate and tone of River Garden. This tone is also
transmitted through the caring and encouragement of a professional and support staff of 180 people, providing services 24 hours a day, seven days a week,
365 days a year. The families of residents, our dedicated Volunteers, and the whole Jewish Community complete this living cycle through active involvement
and support of River Garden. River Garden is outstanding because the people of River Garden are outstanding. Those working for, living in and working in
the Home are special in themselves and towards each other. River Garden gives each and all of us the rare opportunity to express the very best in ourselves.
On behalf of the residents and staff and the Board of Trustees of River Garden we wish the entire commmunity a New Year of Health, growth achievement
and joy. L’SHONO TOVAH

This year the Auxiliary helped replenish linens, provide new dishes for a trayline service that enables the residents’ meals to reach the various floors at the
appropriate temperature. The trayline also facilitates delivery of special individualized diets.
The Auxiliary strives to create a home like atmosphere and, in addition, sponsor entertainment for, and with the residents, such as Bingo, Hobby Shop, Art
classes and “Little Theatre” Groups.
Holidays are always special occasions as the Auxiliary sponsors holiday parties and entertainment for the enjoyment of the Home’s residents.
We welcome community support and participation in the Auxiliary and hope that the coming year will bring peace and happiness throughout the world.

Simhat Torah Honorees
The Festival of Sukkot reaches its joyous climax
on Simhat Torah, the last day of the Holiday. Simhat
Torah is the happiest holiday on the Jewish calendar
because we celebrate our joy and pleasure with the
Torah.
Because of Israel’s perennial love of the Torah,
it has been referred to in Jewish tradition as Israel’s
“bride.” A tradition evolved in ancient times to honor
the individual called for the last reading of the Torah
—the Hatan Torah or the groom of the Torah. The
person honored to begin the Torah reading from its
beginning is called Hatan Bereshit the groom of
Genesis. We also honor a woman who has .made a dis¬
tinctive contribution to our Synagogue and to Jewish
life in general—the “Woman of Valor” honor. We
will honor these individuals at Services on Simhat
Torah morning, Wednesday, October 21.
EUGENE HENRY
A
JPr mm
GENE KORNBLUM
MARSHA L. POLLOCK
Eugene Henry will be honored
as Hatan Torah, the groom of the
Torah. It is an honor truly merited
and deserved.
He has faithfully served on the
Religious Committee, Center Board
and the Board of Trustees for over
thirty years.
His personal devotion and com¬
mitment to Jewish values is dem¬
onstrated by his participation in
daily minyan and Shabbat and
holiday services.
Jack Becker, a friend to Eugene
Henry for many years, describes
him as an “outstanding, devoted,
honest and learned man.” They
have spent many hours of Torah
study together and Jack is impress¬
ed with Eugene’s desire for Jewish
learning.
We are pleased to honor this
man of gentleness and quiet devo¬
tion which earned him the love and
respect of his fellow congregants.
His wife Teresa, members of his
family and the entire Jewish Com¬
munity are justly proud of our
Groom of the Torah.
We look forward to many more
years in which Eugene Henry will
provide inspiration to the Center
Members by his faithful attendance
at the Daily Minyan and all re¬
ligious services.

is very demanding and requires a

Daily /I\ÍQyai)
The Jacksonville Jewish Center takes pride in its Daily Minyan. Through the tireless
efforts of the captains and co-captains, we have minyans every morning and evening.
The anniversary date of the passing of a loved one presents an opportunity to observe a
Mitzvah, if not a double Mitzvah.
The Mitzvah of observing the Yahrzeit is obvious - the second Mitzvah is the
opportunity to insure a minyan so that others, besides yourself, can also observe or
attend a service for their own reasons.
The Daily Minyan needs you. For a satisfying and rewarding experience, attend once or
twice a month on a regular basis.
If you plan to attend, call the captain of the day and time.

Congregational Trip to Israel
Bob and Marlene Bossen
We went home again-though we’d never been there before. What a thrill to walk down the ramp of the huge El A1 jetliner and
touch the hallowed ground of Israel for the first time. We stood quietly for a while, letting the idea of being in Eretz Israel sink in.
We felt awed by our good fortune and that feeling is still with us.
We were home again though we’d not been here before. The sense of pride, the feelings of joy and happiness, the spirit of
adventure as we explored the relics of our ancient history and observed the people of today who appeared to be still cloaked in
the aura of their ancestors glory.
Walking the streets of Jerusalem was an exciting experience yet we felt a sense of calmness and peace. Even with the tensions
of the times we were at ease because the total atmosphere made us feel that the spirit of God was there and no harm would come
to us.
The contrast between the ancient and the modern was ever-present reminding us constantly of what was, and what it has
become and making us dream of what it could be. Such a tiny country - with so much to see and do! And we did it! The Wall,
Masada, the Dead Sea, the enemy borders with their soldiers staring at us behind their poised guns, military manuevers, the
Kibbutzim, the Sinai which is no longer ours and Yammit which no longer exists.
And how do you describe the thrill of Shabbat services in Jerusalem -- singing the same songs and reciting the same prayers as
we do in Jacksonville? And the joy of wearing your Kipah everywhere you go and having Kosher food in every restaurant and
sidewalk cafe. The heartwarming pleasure of being Jewish 24 hours every day!
And as we boarded the plane for Jacksonville we still felt happy and proud and contented because we had been home again
though we’d never been there before ... or had we?!
Ben Gurion Airport, Tel Aviv. With our hearts
pounding and tears of joy we take our first steps
on Israeli soil.
Our first dinner. Disengoff Street in Tel Aviv.
Hungarian style sidewalk restaurant with great
potato blintzes and vegetable soup.
High up on the steps of the ampitheater in
Caesarea we learned how our ancestors
struggled for survival when the Romans ruled
Palestine.
We spent a night on a Kibbutz outside Haifa. The
sign over the main entrance tells it all.
We sit in the remains of the synagogue high atop
the Masada and hear of the courageous battle for
survival by a small band of heroic Jews.
We visited a military outpost on the Syrian
border. The weather was cold but the feelings
among our group and the soldiers were very
warm.
Rabbi Gaffney performs the “toe-tester” method
to determine that the Dead Sea is cold! Some of
our group are floating in the water behind him.
Imagine! Over two thousand years ago our
ancestors stood on these very steps to the
southern Wall of the Temple Mount!
As we left for the airport we made our last stop at
the “Wall.” As did Rabbi Gaffney, we all gave
thanks for a marvelous experience and prayed for
lasting peace in the future.
Those who participated in the Congregation Tour to Israel: Mr. and Mrs. Sidney Berkowitz, Mr. and Mrs. Jack Silverman, Dr. and Mrs. Michael Greenburg, Mr.
and Mrs. Philip Shapiro, Mr. and Mrs. Robert Bossen, Mrs. Freda Isenberg, Dr. Cheryl Rosenblatt, Rabbi and Mrs. David Gaffney, Mrs. Sarah Bossen and Miss
Karen Bossen.

Torah Readers
TORAH READING, THE TEST OF TIME
Among the attributes of God described in Exodus is: “slow to anger” interpreted to
mean affording opportunities for improvement. In chaotic times when traditional values
are ostentatiously breached, we need the synagogue to help direct our lives. Its
atmosphere, ideals and rituals provide a strong influence for family unity and personal
achievement. Opportunities to lead the service or read special portions provide for
personal growth and recognition. The total gamut of celebrations recognize individual
worth and dignity.
We are thankful to many people, young and old, who have devoted so much of their
time to the more arduous task of learning the varied Torah and Haftorah readings. Their
names are recorded in the first column of the weekly Bulletin. They have helped to
maintain Judaism's high standard of study as a way of life. We hope they will always enjoy
the fruits of their labors.
Ted Gross
The following pupils joined the team of Torah Readers this year.

Message from the Administrative Director
Dear Friends,
As I look at the beauty of our newly renovated Sanctuary, complete with the
Ark created by the vision and talent of Israeli artist, Ami Shamir, I am filled with a
sense of holiness and awe in the knowledge that such beauty will inspire our
congregation for many years to come.
I am proud that I had the privilege to be a part of the design committee,
chaired by Philip Selber, whose commitment and dedication to this project
never ceased until its completion.
We look forward to a challenging New Year as we continue with the many diversified activities that are offered in our
Synagogue Center. The finest facilities are available for all occasions -- weddings, Bar and Bat Mitzvahs, social events, sports,
youth, adult education and activities, complete with catering to suit your needs whether large or small.
In closing may I remind you that our Center is not just a building - it is a living, thriving, warm and friendly place of worship and
activity. However, it needs input from all to make it grow. Share your ideas and talents by volunteering to do your part. A call to
the office and our capable staff will find the right spot for you.
My husband, Louis, joins me in a wish for peace and a good year to the entire congregation.
Blanche Slott,
Administrative Director

CALENDAR 225
From the Editor:
“What you see is what you get” may be hackneyed expression, but it describes part of the
purpose behind the Center Yearbook . . . for what you see and read in it, IS what each
member gets. But there is more, much more . . . , the inspiration, the friendships, the
satisfaction and pride from volunteering, the sense of belonging are as much a part of this
book as are the pictures and words.
I want to thank the synagogue leaders and all the volunteers for making possible all the
wonderful programs the Center has to offer. There are also silent supporters who are
always there too.
As the interior of our building begins to take shape one can easily sense the excitement
and anticipation. How wonderful it is to see our dream become a reality.
This has been another banner year for our Synagogue-Center. I look forward to another
inspiring and stimulating year and hope to share many simchas with all of you.
I would like to thank everyone responsible for making this yearbook possible. This is a
joint effort that takes a great deal of work and co-operation. I hope you enjoy reading this
volume as much as Esther Fishier and I had compiling it.
To all of you, I wish a very happy, healthy and prosperous New Year.
L’ Shana Tovah

Class Bet ITS »
The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3 * 7 and provides an
elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting twice during the week and on Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on Hebrew
Reading, Jewish Social Studies, and current events relating to Israel are discussed thoroughly. Synagogue skills, holiday
observances and knowledge of prayers are all part of the comprehensive After Hebrew School program.

To my sister Jewess,
Women’s American ORT is the most complex, exciting, dynamic and fastest growing Jewish women’s organization in the U.S.
We are an activist group not only taking stands, but positively working to upgrade the quality of life for ourselves, our families and
our communities.
We are very involved in public education as well as career and vocation education. Not only have we our first school (highly
acclaimed) in New York and a second school about to open in Los Angeles, but we are most excited about the new Jewish High
School in North Miami where ORT has been asked not only to run the science and technological tracts, but also to help create
the total curriculum!
Not only have we 800 installations of various types of schools in 24 countries on five continents with two million student
graduates in our 102 year history; not only are we known as the finest vocational educators in the world; not only does our
government recognize our expertise, call on our testimony before congressional committees and have ORT members on
educational governmental boards on every echelon of government but we are ... take stands ... and act to uphold the right of
abortion, fight for passage of the ERA, work for human rights and freedom of movement for all peoples, especially Soviet Jewry
and support Israel Americans and Jews (half of our ORT network of schools are there.) We confront this new radical right
movement head on, fighting against censorship, prayer in schools, right to life through anti-democratic and anti-pluralistic views.
Most importantly, we have assumed a vanguard role to thwart anti-Semitism where it raises its ugly head.
This, very briefly, is our program. Our chapters are as pluralistic as our country. Their diversity creates the right place for you
to have your voice heard on the most momentous issues of our harried times and our 600 members in Jacksonville and 145,000 in
the U.S. help give you strength to make your voice heard - loud and clear!
Won’t you make Women’s American ORT stronger? Can you afford in all conscience not to belong?
ORTistically, Sandy Miller
B’nai B’rith
Youth Organization
The B’nai B’rith Youth Organization (BBYO) is the largest high school
Jewish youth organization in the country. It is successful because it
reaches out to every and any Jewish youth, no matter what sect of
Judaism he follows.
The core of the program, Leadership Training, provides knowledge and
skills in a congenial social atmosphere. Inherent in the organization is a
demand for commitment and involvement; the fiber that holds Jewish
youth together no matter how small or large the community.
If you are interested and would like to get involved in Jacksonville’s
AZA/BBG chapters just call Barbara Sherman 737-2564 or Tom Foster
268-9644.
AZA Officers: Tom Foster, Lewis Levy, Mike Armel, Ronnie
Burman and David Burman.

===== PAGE 255 =====
HAROLD
ORBACH
This year the Jacksonville Jewish Center as well as the entire community enjoyed the talents of a
variety of musical performing artists. The PERFORMING ARTIST SERIES was co-ordinated by very
capable Sylvia Shorstein and Sybil Ansbacher and assisted by Isabel Balotin. This series was the first of
its kind to be presented by the Center. We thank the Patrons, Sponsors and everyone who supported
this endeavor . . . you made it a success!!!
The rich, enchanting voice of Cantor Harold Orbach initiated the
Performing Artist Series with the beauty of his remarkable tenor voice.
His varied repetoire delighted the audience. We are very grateful to the
Levin Family who sponsored Cantor Orbach in memory of Harriette
Levin.
Pianist Yefim Bronfman’s playing has been described as “remarkable”.
For all those who attended his performance, it was an evening of fine
music. Mr. Bronfman combined all the exuberance and vigor of a young
virtuoso with the insight and maturity of an established master.
YEFIM
BRONFMAN
American Ballalika Company
Four talented entertainers, who have been called “gypsies” danced, sang and
played a variety of unusual instruments, including the Balalaika. The lavish
costumes, lively vocals and efferevescent personalities added to the evening’s
excitement.
Arthur Siegel
Broadway pianist and composer, Arthur Siegel
brought back the beauty and delightful quality of the
“old songs.” Mr. Siegel stirred memories when he
sang his own composition “Love is a Simple Thing.”
We thank Eddie Siegel and his family for their support.

===== PAGE 259 =====
Let its go with our young and old . . .
with our sons and daughters . . .
to worship God on our festival.
Exodus 10:9
Passover at the Jacksonville Jewish Center has been a most meaningful time
for adults and children of all ages. Passover, the Time of our Freedom has
become a time when we have Built Bridges . .. Brought together generations...
families and friends.
Young and old come together in the synagogues and homes to celebrate this
festive holiday.
Shown on these pages are children of our schools leading and participating in
a model Seder.
PASSOVER FOR ALL PROJECT
“Let all who are hungry come to eat” is recited during the Seder when the Matzah is
uncovered. To insure that all will be able to partake of Passover, the young people of each
school at the Jewish Center undertook a most meaningful project. Each student was
requested to bring one dollar ($1.00) to school. These monies were used to purchase food
stuffs for gift boxes to be given to those families who, at this time, were unable to provide the
foods of the holiday for themselves. Please help our young people with this project when
they call you next Passover.
Members from each class were selected to purchase the food and the older students
helped deliver them.
PASSOVER FOR ALL
209
===== PAGE 260 =====
Sunday Sports Basketball
The S.S.A. Basketball program finished its 8-week season on Sunday, February 28th, with final game and the presentation of
awards. Trophies were given to all players in League One, Two and Three. League Four received gold and silver medallions on
red, white and blue ribbons.
One hundred and ten boys and girls participated in this popular athletic program, with emphasis on fun, participation,
sportsmanship and skill improvement.
A special thank you goes to all of the wonderful coaches who contributed so much to the program!
